        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

      response:
        output: >-

          Understanding how genes interact with each other in specific contexts
          to perform their functions is crucial for identifying the genetic
          factors involved in complex traits. Gene-gene interactions have been
          shown to be critical for disease origin and progression, but
          traditional methods of analyzing gene expression data have limitations
          in identifying these interactions. In this study, we present
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that combines transcriptome-wide
          association studies and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for joint analysis. This approach uses
          modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions to map gene-trait associations, enabling us to
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. We demonstrate the accuracy of PhenoPLIER
          in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action, and we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation to
          further validate our approach. By incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the lens of gene modules, which has important
          implications for drug repurposing and the development of new
          therapies. Our findings highlight the importance of considering gene
          interactions in complex trait analysis and provide a valuable resource
          for researchers working in this field.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

      response:
        output: >-

          Complex traits are the result of interactions between multiple genes,
          and determining how these genes influence these traits requires an
          understanding of expression regulation across different conditions.
          While transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify
          individual genes associated with disease-relevant mechanisms, modern
          models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease etiology. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation
          for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
          with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our
          results show that diseases are significantly associated with gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types and that our approach
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of
          action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we found that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. Our findings demonstrate that PhenoPLIER provides a novel
          framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules and can contextualize these associations to reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. By incorporating
          groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can help uncover disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms, leading to new therapeutic
          opportunities.

      response:
        output: >-

          Genes play a complex and interdependent role in the functioning of
          organisms. Understanding how these genes influence disease and
          therapeutic responses requires an understanding of expression
          regulation across different contexts. While transcriptome-wide
          association studies have helped identify individual genes associated
          with disease, recent models predict that gene-gene interactions are
          crucial in disease etiology and progression. In this study, we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene
          expression patterns, pharmacological perturbation data, and trait
          associations into a common latent representation for joint analysis.
          By clustering genes with similar expression profiles across the same
          conditions, we observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately
          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action.
          Moreover, using CRISPR screening, we find that functionally important
          players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
          modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework
          for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules
          and can contextualize single-gene strategies in complex traits.

      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          The study of genes and their interactions in disease development is a
          crucial aspect of modern medical research. However, the complexity of
          these interactions has made it difficult to identify specific genes
          that are responsible for certain diseases. Recent advances in
          functional genomics and transcriptome-wide association studies have
          shed light on this issue by providing new insights into gene
          expression patterns and their associations with disease etiology.
          However, these approaches often rely on single-gene analyses, which
          can miss the broader picture of how groups of co-expressed genes
          interact to contribute to complex traits.


          In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
          maps gene expression patterns and pharmacological perturbation data
          into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
          representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression
          patterns across the same conditions. We show that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease
          pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we use a CRISPR
          screen to analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally
          important players lack associations but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.


          Our findings demonstrate the importance of considering groups of
          co-expressed genes in the context of disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms. By providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the lens of gene modules, PhenoPLIER can help
          identify potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. This
          approach has significant implications for future therapeutic
          development and may lead to new insights into the underlying causes of
          complex diseases. Overall, our findings highlight the importance of
          integrating functional genomics and gene expression data to better
          understand disease mechanisms and identify new drug targets.

          Genes work in harmony with each other within specific contexts to
          perform their functions. Understanding how these genes contribute to
          complex traits requires a deeper understanding of expression
          regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is crucial for
          developing new therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped identify individual genes associated with
          disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of complex trait
          architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in
          disease etiology and progression. In this study, we present
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that combines gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We found that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we identified functionally important players lacking
          associations but prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and reveals
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our approach
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/phenoplier/prompts/candidate.txt

        output: >-

          Genetic studies have long been a crucial tool in understanding disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms. Functional genomics has enabled us to
          analyze gene expression patterns and identify potential therapeutic
          targets. However, the complexity of traits and the importance of
          gene-gene interactions in disease origin and progression require a
          more nuanced approach. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
          tool that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
          analysis. By mapping genes with similar expression patterns across
          different conditions, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
          associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
          strategies. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          highlighting the importance of grouping genes with similar expression
          patterns in understanding disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

        output: >-

          Gene expression patterns are critical in determining how genes
          function together to produce complex traits. However, uncovering the
          underlying mechanisms of disease-relevant mechanisms has been a
          challenge for genetic studies. Modern models predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression,
          but transcriptome-wide association studies have not fully captured
          this complexity. To overcome this challenge, we introduce PhenoPLIER,
          a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation
          for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
          with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We
          observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
          expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts
          known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
          Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation and
          find that functionally important players lack associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our findings
          suggest that by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel
          framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules.

      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          Complex traits, such as cancer and cardiovascular diseases, are
          influenced by multiple genetic and environmental factors. The
          mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across different
          conditions is crucial for developing new therapies. Traditional
          transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify individual
          genes associated with disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models predict that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in
          disease etiology and progression. Therefore, there is a need to
          develop computational approaches that can map gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a common representation for
          joint analysis.


          We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation based on modules of genes with similar
          expression patterns across the same conditions. Our results show that
          diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in
          relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.


          In addition to disease associations, we applied PhenoPLIER to analyze
          lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen. We found that functionally
          important players lack associations but were prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings suggest that by
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies.


          In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, which is
          crucial for identifying therapeutic targets and repurposing drugs in
          complex diseases. Our approach can be used to map genetic associations
          onto disease etiology and progression mechanisms, enabling the
          discovery of new drug candidates for complex diseases.

          In the complex world of gene regulation, individual genes work in
          concert with each other to perform their functions. However,
          understanding how these genes influence complex traits requires a
          detailed analysis of expression regulation across various conditions.
          Such insights are critical for developing new therapies that can
          target specific disease mechanisms. While transcriptome-wide
          association studies have been instrumental in identifying single gene
          associations with diseases, the modern models of complex trait
          architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role
          in disease development and progression. In this study, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that uses gene co-expression
          modules to map genetic associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. We
          observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
          expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
          predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. This suggests that by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. In conclusion,
          PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the lens of gene modules, which may help uncover
          new therapeutic targets and mechanisms of action in complex diseases.

          Complex traits such as diseases are determined by the concerted
          activity of multiple genes, which makes their functional genomics a
          challenging task. Gene co-expression analysis has emerged as a
          promising approach for understanding disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression, which poses a
          significant challenge to the current single-gene strategies. To
          overcome this limitation, we developed PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that maps gene expression patterns, pharmacological
          perturbation data, and gene-trait associations into a common latent
          representation for joint analysis. Our analysis revealed that diseases
          are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
          cell types, and our approach accurately predicted known drug-disease
          pairs and inferred mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR

          associations but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by

          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          enabling us to contextualize gene expression patterns and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our findings
          highlight the importance of functional genomics in uncovering disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms, and provide insights into the
          development of new therapeutic targets.

          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in

          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with

          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >-

          The current research gap in the field of genetic studies is the need
          for a computational approach that can accurately map gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. Genes act in concert with
          each other in specific contexts to perform their functions, and
          determining how these genes influence complex traits requires a
          mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across different
          conditions. The importance of this insight cannot be overstated, as it
          has been shown to be critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. To
          address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our
          method is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns
          across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER's novel framework provides an
          accurate way to contextualize genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
          strategies, thereby advancing our understanding of disease etiology
          and drug mechanisms.

          We present PhenoPLIER, a computational tool that integrates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
          latent space for joint analysis. Genes work together in specific
          contexts to perform their functions, making it crucial to understand
          expression regulation across different conditions to determine how
          genes influence complex traits. While transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped identify individual gene roles in disease-relevant
          mechanisms, modern models of complex trait architecture suggest that
          gene-gene interactions are critical in disease etiology and
          progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of

          are associated with relevant cell type-expressed gene modules, and our

          mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for lipid

          PhenoPLIER. Our results demonstrate that by incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations
          and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. In
          summary, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation

          In this manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that bridges the gap between genetic studies and functional genomics
          by mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. We
          address the challenge of understanding how genes work together in
          specific contexts to perform their functions, which is critical for
          developing new therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease

          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
          Moreover, we demonstrate that PhenoPLIER can prioritize functionally
          important players lacking associations but included in
          trait-associated modules. In conclusion, by contextualizing genetic

          framework for interpreting complex trait etiology and drug mechanisms.
          Our approach has broader significance as it facilitates the discovery
          of therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies and informs
          drug repurposing efforts.

          In the field of genetic studies, functional genomics has emerged as a
          powerful tool for understanding complex traits and disease mechanisms.
          Gene co-expression analysis provides valuable insights into the
          molecular pathways involved in various diseases, but identifying
          therapeutic targets based on individual genes can be challenging due
          to the lack of a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
          across different conditions. To address this gap, we developed
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
          representation for joint analysis. By utilizing modules of genes with
          similar expression patterns across the same conditions, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. Our results show that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
          and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          and our approach can help identify new therapeutic targets and inform
          drug repurposing efforts in complex diseases.

          co-expression patterns associated with disease etiology and drug

          associated with specific gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Moreover, we used a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation and found that functionally important players
          lacking associations were prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. Our findings highlight the importance of contextualizing
          genetic associations through gene module analysis, which can reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Overall, our study
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations and
          identifying therapeutic targets through gene modules.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          The study of genes and their interactions has been critical in
          understanding the etiology of complex diseases. However, determining
          how these genes act together to produce disease outcomes requires a
          more comprehensive analysis of gene expression patterns across

          PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic

          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across

          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a

          Genes function in a coordinated manner with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. A mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions is critical for
          determining how these genes influence complex traits and developing
          new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
          identified the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          crucial role in disease origin and progression. In this study, we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. The representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions, which we observe to be significantly associated with
          diseases in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a
          CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally
          important players lack associations but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our findings suggest that
          understanding the genetic architecture of complex traits through gene
          co-expression analysis can help identify therapeutic targets and
          facilitate drug repurposing.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by

          Genetic studies and functional genomics have identified many genes
          associated with disease, but determining the underlying mechanisms of
          disease is a complex task. Gene co-expression analysis has shown that
          genes work together to regulate expression patterns across different
          conditions. However, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. To address this
          gap, we developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for joint analysis. We found that
          diseases are significantly associated with modules of genes expressed
          in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
          using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found that

          in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results provide insight
          into disease etiology and drug mechanisms, highlighting the importance
          of gene co-expression analysis for drug repurposing and clustering of
          complex traits.

          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of the
          architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. In this study,
          we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
          based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we find that functionally important
          players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
          modules by PhenoPLIER using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation. Our findings highlight the importance of gene
          co-expression in identifying therapeutic targets and drug repurposing.

          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

            namedScores: *ref_0
            text: >-

              Understanding how genes interact with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions is crucial for identifying the
              genetic factors involved in complex traits. Gene-gene interactions
              have been shown to be critical for disease origin and progression,
              but traditional methods of analyzing gene expression data have
              limitations in identifying these interactions. In this study, we
              present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that combines
              transcriptome-wide association studies and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. This approach uses modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions to map gene-trait
              associations, enabling us to contextualize genetic associations
              and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. We
              demonstrate the accuracy of PhenoPLIER in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action, and we use
              a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation to further validate
              our approach. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules, which has important
              implications for drug repurposing and the development of new
              therapies. Our findings highlight the importance of considering
              gene interactions in complex trait analysis and provide a valuable
              resource for researchers working in this field.

              The study of genes and their interactions in disease development
              is a crucial aspect of modern medical research. However, the
              complexity of these interactions has made it difficult to identify
              specific genes that are responsible for certain diseases. Recent
              advances in functional genomics and transcriptome-wide association
              studies have shed light on this issue by providing new insights
              into gene expression patterns and their associations with disease
              etiology. However, these approaches often rely on single-gene
              analyses, which can miss the broader picture of how groups of
              co-expressed genes interact to contribute to complex traits.


              In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
              that maps gene expression patterns and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We show
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation and find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.


              Our findings demonstrate the importance of considering groups of
              co-expressed genes in the context of disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms. By providing a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, PhenoPLIER
              can help identify potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. This approach has significant implications for future
              therapeutic development and may lead to new insights into the
              underlying causes of complex diseases. Overall, our findings
              highlight the importance of integrating functional genomics and
              gene expression data to better understand disease mechanisms and
              identify new drug targets.

            text: >-

              Genetic studies have long been a crucial tool in understanding
              disease etiology and drug mechanisms. Functional genomics has
              enabled us to analyze gene expression patterns and identify
              potential therapeutic targets. However, the complexity of traits
              and the importance of gene-gene interactions in disease origin and
              progression require a more nuanced approach. Here we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational tool that integrates gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for joint analysis. By mapping genes with
              similar expression patterns across different conditions,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, highlighting the importance of grouping genes with
              similar expression patterns in understanding disease etiology and
              drug mechanisms.

              Gene expression patterns are critical in determining how genes
              function together to produce complex traits. However, uncovering
              the underlying mechanisms of disease-relevant mechanisms has been
              a challenge for genetic studies. Modern models predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression, but transcriptome-wide association studies have not
              fully captured this complexity. To overcome this challenge, we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
              we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation and find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our
              findings suggest that by incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.
              Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              Complex traits, such as cancer and cardiovascular diseases, are
              influenced by multiple genetic and environmental factors. The
              mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
              different conditions is crucial for developing new therapies.
              Traditional transcriptome-wide association studies have helped
              identify individual genes associated with disease-relevant
              mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a significant role in disease etiology and
              progression. Therefore, there is a need to develop computational
              approaches that can map gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common representation for
              joint analysis.


              We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our
              results show that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms
              of action.


              In addition to disease associations, we applied PhenoPLIER to
              analyze lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen. We found that
              functionally important players lack associations but were
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These
              findings suggest that by incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.


              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, which is crucial for identifying therapeutic targets and
              repurposing drugs in complex diseases. Our approach can be used to
              map genetic associations onto disease etiology and progression
              mechanisms, enabling the discovery of new drug candidates for
              complex diseases.

              In the complex world of gene regulation, individual genes work in
              concert with each other to perform their functions. However,
              understanding how these genes influence complex traits requires a
              detailed analysis of expression regulation across various
              conditions. Such insights are critical for developing new
              therapies that can target specific disease mechanisms. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in
              identifying single gene associations with diseases, the modern
              models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease development and
              progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a

              genetic associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a

              suggests that by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. In conclusion,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules, which may help
              uncover new therapeutic targets and mechanisms of action in

              Complex traits such as diseases are determined by the concerted
              activity of multiple genes, which makes their functional genomics
              a challenging task. Gene co-expression analysis has emerged as a
              promising approach for understanding disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression, which poses a significant challenge to the current
              single-gene strategies. To overcome this limitation, we developed
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene expression
              patterns, pharmacological perturbation data, and gene-trait
              associations into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. Our analysis revealed that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach accurately predicted known drug-disease pairs and
              inferred mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen,
              we identified functionally important players that lacked
              associations but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, enabling us to contextualize gene expression patterns and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our
              findings highlight the importance of functional genomics in
              uncovering disease etiology and drug mechanisms, and provide
              insights into the development of new therapeutic targets.

              The manuscript presents PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach
              that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. This method takes into account the concerted action of
              genes in specific contexts to perform their functions. It is
              critical to understand expression regulation across different
              conditions to determine how these genes influence complex traits.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, but
              modern models predict that gene-gene interactions are crucial for
              disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is
              based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
              the same conditions. The approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, a
              CRISPR screen analyzing lipid regulation shows that functionally

              through the lens of gene modules, which can contextualize
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. This approach has implications for therapeutic target
              discovery and drug repurposing, highlighting disease etiology and
              mechanisms.

            text: >-

              The current research gap in the field of genetic studies is the
              need for a computational approach that can accurately map
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. Genes act in
              concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
              functions, and determining how these genes influence complex
              traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. The importance of this
              insight cannot be overstated, as it has been shown to be critical
              for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
              studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. To address
              this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
              maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
              into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our method
              is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns
              across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.
              Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER's novel framework provides an accurate way
              to contextualize genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies, thereby advancing our understanding of disease
              etiology and drug mechanisms.

              ---


              We present PhenoPLIER, a computational tool that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a unified latent space for joint analysis. Genes work together in
              specific contexts to perform their functions, making it crucial to
              understand expression regulation across different conditions to
              determine how genes influence complex traits. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify
              individual gene roles in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern
              models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene
              interactions are critical in disease etiology and progression.
              PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of co-expressed
              genes across the same conditions. We find that diseases are
              associated with relevant cell type-expressed gene modules, and our
              approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for lipid
              regulation, we identify functionally important players that lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. Our results demonstrate that by incorporating groups
              of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. In summary, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules.

              ---


              In this manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that bridges the gap between genetic studies and
              functional genomics by mapping gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. We address the challenge of
              understanding how genes work together in specific contexts to
              perform their functions, which is critical for developing new
              therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association studies have
              helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms,
              modern models of complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease etiology and
              progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of
              genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions.
              Our findings show that diseases are significantly associated with
              gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms
              of action. Moreover, we demonstrate that PhenoPLIER can prioritize
              functionally important players lacking associations but included
              in trait-associated modules. In conclusion, by contextualizing

              mechanisms. Our approach has broader significance as it
              facilitates the discovery of therapeutic targets missed by
              single-gene strategies and informs drug repurposing efforts.

              ---


              We present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data to create a common latent representation for
              joint analysis. Genes often act synergistically in specific
              contexts to carry out their functions. Understanding how these
              genes contribute to complex traits requires an understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions, which has been
              critical in developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have helped identify individual genes
              associated with disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict
              that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in disease origin
              and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules
              of genes that exhibit similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions. We demonstrate that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              inferring mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR
              screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally
              important players lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These results highlight
              the importance of incorporating groups of co-expressed genes for
              contextualizing genetic associations and identifying potential
              targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a
              new framework for interpreting genetic associations through the
              lens of gene modules.

              Context: Genetic studies have long sought to understand the role

              that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease

              Content: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
              maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
              into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our method
              is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns
              across the same conditions and can accurately predict known
              drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action. We applied our
              approach to lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen, revealing that
              functionally important players were prioritized in
              trait-associated modules despite lacking associations.


              Conclusion: By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our approach
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, which has broader significance
              in drug discovery and repurposing. Overall, our findings highlight
              the importance of considering gene-gene interactions in disease
              etiology and therapeutic target identification.

              utilizes modules of genes with similar expression patterns across

            text: >-

              In the field of genetic studies, functional genomics has emerged
              as a powerful tool for understanding complex traits and disease
              mechanisms. Gene co-expression analysis provides valuable insights
              into the molecular pathways involved in various diseases, but
              identifying therapeutic targets based on individual genes can be
              challenging due to the lack of a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. To address this
              gap, we developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. By utilizing
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our
              results show that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms
              of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, and our approach can help identify new therapeutic
              targets and inform drug repurposing efforts in complex diseases.

              traits, but the underlying mechanisms of these associations are
              not fully understood. To address this challenge, we developed a

              co-expression patterns associated with disease etiology and drug

              therapeutic targets through gene modules.
