            text: >-

              Genetic studies and functional genomics have identified numerous
              disease-associated genetic variants, but their functional
              significance is often unclear. To address this gap in the
              literature, our study used gene co-expression patterns to
              contextualize genetic associations and identify potential drug
              targets. We applied a novel approach called PhenoPLIER, which
              clustered genes based on their expression profiles across multiple
              cell types and conditions. Our results showed that diseases were
              significantly associated with specific modules of co-expressed
              genes in relevant cell types, and we used this information to
              predict known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action.
              Additionally, we analyzed lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen
              and found that functionally important players lacked associations
              but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.
              Overall, our findings demonstrate the potential of PhenoPLIER to
              provide a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, which may lead to new
              therapeutic targets and improved drug repurposing strategies.

              understanding the etiology of complex diseases. However,

              outcomes requires a more comprehensive analysis of gene expression
              patterns across different conditions. In this manuscript, we

              specific traits and diseases. Our results show that by grouping

              genes, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of functional genomics,

              treatment.

              Genes function in a coordinated manner with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. A mechanistic understanding
              of expression regulation across different conditions is critical
              for determining how these genes influence complex traits and
              developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association
              studies have identified the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. The representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, which we observe to be significantly associated with
              diseases in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
              known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our
              findings suggest that understanding the genetic architecture of
              complex traits through gene co-expression analysis can help
              identify therapeutic targets and facilitate drug repurposing.

            text: >-

              The study of disease etiology and drug mechanisms requires a
              comprehensive understanding of gene expression patterns. While
              individual genes have been shown to play a role in disease, recent
              models predict that gene-gene interactions are critical for the
              development and progression of complex traits. To address this gap
              in the literature, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation. This allows
              for a joint analysis of gene expression patterns across different
              conditions. We found that diseases are significantly associated
              with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
              approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we used a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and found that functionally important
              players were prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER, even if they lacked direct associations. Overall, our
              study highlights the importance of gene co-expression in
              understanding disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

            text: >-

              Genetic studies and functional genomics have identified many genes
              associated with disease, but determining the underlying mechanisms
              of disease is a complex task. Gene co-expression analysis has
              shown that genes work together to regulate expression patterns
              across different conditions. However, modern models predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. To address this gap, we developed PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. We found that diseases are
              significantly associated with modules of genes expressed in
              relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found that
              functionally important players lack associations but were
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results
              provide insight into disease etiology and drug mechanisms,
              highlighting the importance of gene co-expression analysis for
              drug repurposing and clustering of complex traits.

              The coordinated action of genes in specific contexts is essential
              for their functioning. Understanding how these genes influence
              complex traits requires an insight into the regulation of
              expression across different conditions. The role of individual
              genes in disease-relevant mechanisms has been uncovered through
              transcriptome-wide association studies. However, recent models
              predict that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in
              disease origin and progression. To address this challenge, we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings show
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation,
              we find that functionally important players lack associations but
              are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These
              results highlight the importance of gene-gene interactions in
              disease etiology and drug mechanisms and provide insights into
              therapeutic targets and drug repurposing.

            text: >-

              Genetic studies have revolutionized our understanding of complex
              traits and disease mechanisms. However, individual gene
              associations with complex traits only provide a partial picture of
              the underlying molecular processes. To bridge this gap, functional
              genomics techniques are increasingly being used to study gene
              expression patterns across different conditions. These studies
              reveal that genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts, making it critical to understand how they influence
              complex traits. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. By leveraging modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions, our approach reveals
              significant disease associations with specific cell types and
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using CRISPR screens to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lacking
              associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER, highlighting the potential for drug repurposing and
              therapeutic target discovery. Overall, our work provides a
              powerful tool for identifying new disease biomarkers and drug
              candidates through the analysis of gene expression patterns and
              functional genomics data.

            text: >-

              In the field of functional genomics, genes work together to carry
              out specific functions in various contexts. In order to understand
              how these genes impact complex traits, it is essential to have a
              comprehensive understanding of their expression regulation across
              different conditions. This knowledge has been shown to be critical
              for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
              studies have helped identify individual genes involved in
              disease-relevant mechanisms, but recent models of complex trait
              architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a crucial
              role in disease onset and progression. In this manuscript, we
              present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that links gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared
              latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is
              based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
              the same conditions. Our results demonstrate that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease
              pairs and infer mechanisms of action. Additionally, we show that
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, functionally
              important players may lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, this study
              highlights the importance of understanding gene expression
              patterns and their impact on complex traits in disease etiology
              and drug mechanisms.

              ---


              In recent years, genetic studies and functional genomics have
              provided valuable insights into disease etiology. However, a
              mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
              different conditions is necessary to determine how genes influence
              complex traits. This knowledge is critical for developing new
              therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
              helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
              mechanisms, modern models of the architecture of complex traits
              predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease
              origin and progression. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for a joint analysis. This representation is based
              on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
              same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs
              and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER using a
              CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation. Our findings highlight
              the importance of gene co-expression in identifying therapeutic
              targets and drug repurposing.

              and follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits
              in a single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely
              necessary to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the
              abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").

            text: >-

              The study of genes and their interactions in specific contexts is
              crucial for understanding complex traits and developing new
              therapies. However, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a critical role in disease origin and
              progression. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. Our approach uses modules of
              genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions
              to accurately predict known drug-disease pairs and infer
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we use PhenoPLIER to analyze
              lipid regulation in a CRISPR screen and find that functionally
              important players lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules. Overall, our study highlights the
              importance of gene-gene interactions in disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms.
